---------- Forwarded message ---------
From: Allen Wo <awo@lunohq.com>
Date: Tue, Dec 8, 2015 at 6:56 PM
Subject: Dec 7 RV Luno data
To: Maghan Cook <mcook@redventures.com>, Chelsea Harrell <
charrell@redventures.com>


Hey Maghan, Chelsea,

The normal weekly data below + a deep dive to try to illuminate the
behavior between the different orgs.

Summary:
- weekly usage bounced back after the holiday week to the 10% baseline that
we were seeing prior.
- the segmented analysis for the month of Nov confirms what I think you
suspected already. There is a gap between Sales and the rest of the org.
Sales is more interested in other people throughout the org, whereas the
rest of the org is not that interested in Sales.

Let me know if you have follow up questions!

Also, I'd love to catch up over video conference before the holidays. I
know this time of year is super busy for you guys, but how's next Wed or
Fri afternoon look for yall?

Cheers,
allen


---

*Week over week unique users since launch*
- Unique users and searchers bounced back after a the holiday week
- 27 unique users (9% of 309 activated users)
- 20 unique users who searched (6% of 309 activated users)

[image: image.png]

*November Analysis*
Here's the high level stats I shared last week. Note: there's a change in
the denominator for the percentage calculations from 302 to 309 b/c we
actually had 7 new users activated in November.
- The main stat I=E2=80=99m tracking is unique users who searched. In Novem=
ber, 23%
(71 out of 309) of the activated base start at least one search.
- 29% of activated users logged on in November (90 out of 309).

[image: image.png]

Here's the unique users by Group in Nov:
- RVPower Sales and Sales Support are more active than Corporate (~25%
retained vs. 15%).
- Note: the 413 number represents the users that were uploaded into Luno
for the pilot. And the 90 number represents the unique users who were
active.
- Sales also looked at more people per user during the month than Sales
Support and Corporate (3.7 vs. 2.7 vs. 1.7)
[image: image.png]

Here's people views by Group in Nov. The main chart contains raw counts in
a pivot table for what each group was viewing, e.g. people in Corporate
looked at Sales profiles 5 times in Nov. The percentage tables to the right
and bottom answer the questions of "who was each group looking at?" and
"who looked at this group?" respectively:
- From the table on the right, in general each group is predominantly
self-interested and looking at others in their own group.
- Sales is curious about Sales Support - 32% of Sales people views were of
people in Sales Support. Conversely, 63% of the views of Sales Support
people came from Sales.
- No one really cares about Sales. Corporate and Sales Support only looked
at Sales 16% and 11% of the time, respectively. Also, only 8% of the views
of Sales people came from Corporate and Sales Support (4% and 4%).

[image: image.png]
